###begin article-title 0
###xml 68 70 64 66 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 104 111 100 107 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 104 111 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Promoter and regulon analysis of nitrogen assimilation factor, sigma54, reveal alternative strategy for E. coli MG1655 flagellar biosynthesis
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 0 1 0 1 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">:</sup>
:Present address: Kai Zhao, Department of Microbiology, Tufts University, 136 Harrison Avenue, Boston, MA 02111, USA.
###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 137 139 129 131 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 149 150 137 138 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N</sup>
###xml 342 358 330 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 417 424 405 412 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 441 443 425 427 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 521 523 497 499 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 752 754 724 726 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 839 841 807 809 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 881 888 849 856 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 342 358 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 881 888 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Bacteria core RNA polymerase (RNAP) must associate with a sigma factor to recognize promoter sequences. Promoters recognized by the sigma54 (or sigmaN) associated RNA polymerase are unique in having conserved positions around -24 and -12 nucleotides upstream from the transcriptional start site. Using DNA microarrays representing the entire Escherichia coli genome and promoter validation approaches, we identify 40 in vivo targets of sigma54, the nitrogen assimilation sigma factor, and estimate that there are 70 sigma54 promoters in total. Immunoprecipitation assays have been performed to further evaluate the efficiency of our approaches. In addition, promoter consensus binding search and primer extension assay helped us to identify a new sigma54 promoter carried by insB-5 in the upstream of flhDC operon. The involvement of sigma54 in flagellar biosynthesis in sequenced E. coli strain MG1655 indicates a fluid gene regulation phenomenon carried by some mobile elements in bacteria genome.
###end p 2
###begin title 3
INTRODUCTION
###end title 3
###begin p 4
The upstream regulatory region of all bacterial genes or operons contains one or more promoter(s). This is a special DNA sequence that can be specifically recognized by the RNA polymerase sigma subunit to allow binding and initiation of transcription. A major mode of gene regulation occurs via the binding of sigma factors to these specific DNA sequences. Sigma factors are identified by their ability to bind to core RNA polymerase (RNAP) and by their ability to direct promoter-specific transcription.
###end p 4
###begin p 5
###xml 4 20 4 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 53 55 45 47 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 130 131 118 119 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 206 213 194 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 247 250 235 238 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B2 B3 B4 B5 B6">2&#8211;6</xref>
###xml 269 276 257 264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 297 299 281 283 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 306 308 286 288 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 315 317 291 293 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 324 325 296 297 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S</sup>
###xml 332 333 300 301 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</sup>
###xml 340 341 304 305 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</sup>
###xml 351 355 311 315 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FecI</sup>
###xml 407 409 363 365 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 431 433 383 385 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 440 442 388 390 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 449 450 393 394 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S</sup>
###xml 457 458 397 398 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</sup>
###xml 465 466 401 402 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</sup>
###xml 476 480 408 412 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fecI</sup>
###xml 495 497 423 425 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 610 611 538 539 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 612 613 540 541 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 744 745 668 669 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 746 748 670 672 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 4 20 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 206 213 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 269 276 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The Escherichia coli housekeeping sigma factor, sigma70, was the first prokaryotic sigma factor to be purified and characterized (1). Since then, numerous sigma factors have been found and characterized in E. coli and other prokaryotic organisms (2-6). The seven known E. coli sigma factors (sigma70, sigma54, sigma32, sigmaS, sigmaF, sigmaE and sigmaFecI) have been categorized into two families. The sigma70 family contains sigma70, sigma32, sigmaS, sigmaF, sigmaE and sigmafecI, whereas sigma54, because of differences in sequence, promoter architecture, and function, is placed in its own separate family (7,8). The intracellular levels of each individual sigma factor change in response to growth transitions and environmental conditions (9,10) that play important roles in the regulation of gene expression.
###end p 5
###begin p 6
###xml 5 7 1 3 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 14 15 6 7 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N</sup>
###xml 14 15 6 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sup>N</sup></italic>
###xml 193 195 185 187 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 203 205 191 193 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 263 270 251 258 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 414 416 390 392 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 431 433 403 405 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 500 502 464 466 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 516 518 476 478 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 587 588 547 548 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 649 651 605 607 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 664 666 620 622 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B12">12</xref>
###xml 667 669 623 625 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 683 685 635 637 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 823 824 775 776 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>
###xml 825 826 777 778 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 902 904 850 852 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 959 964 907 912 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14 B15 B16 B17">14&#8211;17</xref>
###xml 1052 1054 996 998 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1066 1073 1010 1017 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1116 1118 1056 1058 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1142 1149 1082 1089 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1311 1313 1247 1249 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1502 1504 1434 1436 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1681 1683 1609 1611 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1706 1708 1630 1632 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1760 1762 1680 1682 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1860 1862 1776 1778 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1915 1917 1827 1829 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 1917 1925 1829 1837 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 2104 2106 2012 2014 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 2306 2313 2214 2221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 263 270 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1066 1073 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1142 1149 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2306 2313 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
sigma54 (sigmaN) was identified as a sigma factor involved in the transcription of genes involved in the cellular assimilation of ammonia and glutamate under conditions of nitrogen limitation (11). sigma54 is structurally and functionally distinct from the other E. coli sigma factors and shares very little if any sequence similarity with the primary sigma factors. The three major differences that separate sigma54 from the sigma70 family of the other sigma factors are: (i) unlike members of sigma70 family, sigma54 is able to bind promoter DNA in the absence of core RNA polymerase (7); (ii) regulatory proteins like NtrB and NtrC activate sigma54 holoenzyme (12,13); (iii) sigma54 recognizes promoter sequences with conserved GG and GC elements located -24 to -12 nucleotides upstream of the transcription start site (3,7). Although some bioinformatics approaches have been applied to search sigma54 consensus binding site in different bacteria species (14-17), no large-scale experimental effort has been undertaken to unravel in detail the sigma54 regulon in E. coli. Here, we present an updated list of sigma54-dependent promoters in E. coli. Computer programs, such as BioProspector and HMMer, have been utilized together to search and present the derivation of an extended consensus sequence for sigma54 binding. Different from previous computational methods that only focused on the upstream intergenic sequences extracted from the genomes of several bacterial species, we found 18% of sigma54-promoters are located within the coding region of known genes or between convergently transcribed genes. This suggests a previously uncharacterized regulatory function of sigma54. We also compare sigma54-dependent genes identified in this study with sigma70-dependent genes identified in a separate study (our unpublished data). We found that 14% of sigma54-dependent genes can be directly transcribed by sigma70in vitro. This might indicate that bacteria use different promoter organizations to produce different regulatory outcomes in different environments. In addition, we also found a new sigma54-dependent promoter upstream of the flhDC operon in the sequenced strain MG1655 and provide an alternative explanation for the high motility of this sequenced strain compared with its closely related E. coli strains.
###end p 6
###begin title 7
EXPERIMENTAL PROCEDURES
###end title 7
###begin title 8
Reagents, strains and plasmids
###end title 8
###begin p 9
###xml 168 174 168 174 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 176 178 176 178 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 367 368 357 358 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 371 372 361 362 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
All reagents were purchased from Sigma Chemical Company (St Louis, MO, USA) unless otherwise indicated. A 10X MOPS minimal media was prepared as described in Neidhardt et al. (18). The media were filter sterilized through a 0.2 microm filter and stored at 4degreesC. The defined media for log-phase cell growth contained 1x MOPS minimal media, 0.1% glucose, 0.66 mM K2HPO4. Neidhardt's; MOPS-based defined media are now available commercially from Teknova, Inc.
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 12 19 12 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 65 72 65 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 99 100 94 95 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 102 103 97 98 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 108 109 103 104 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 113 114 108 109 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 137 139 132 134 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 238 240 229 231 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 244 251 235 242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 299 301 290 292 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 302 304 293 295 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 353 355 340 342 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 370 372 357 359 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 373 375 360 362 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 430 437 417 424 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 452 456 439 443 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ltet</sub>
###xml 575 577 562 564 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 722 729 709 716 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 12 19 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 65 77 <span type="species:ncbi:83333">E. coli K-12</span>
###xml 244 251 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 722 729 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Because the E. coli Genechip probe set is based on the sequenced E. coli K-12 strain MG1655 (lambda- F- ilvG- rfb-50 rph-1, prototroph) (19), we chose this bacterial strain for use in our study. In order to disrupt the expression of sigma54 in E. coli, we used a simple and highly efficient method (20,21) to prepared in-frame deletion strains for sigma54 as described (22,23). For controllable induction of individual regulators in vivo, we used the PLtet promoter which is controlled by the repressor TetR to construct these overexpression vectors as described previously (23). A downstream gene can be induced in the presence of the inducer anhydrotetracycline (aTc). All strains used in this study were derivatives of E. coli K12 MG1655.
###end p 10
###begin title 11
Growth conditions, preparation of cell lysates
###end title 11
###begin p 12
###xml 357 359 341 343 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 502 504 486 488 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 505 507 489 491 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
All cultures were grown in a New Brunswick Gyrotory water bath shaker (model G76) with vigorous aeration unless otherwise indicated. For cultures of cells carrying antibiotic resistance markers, the media were supplemented with ampicillin (100 microg/ml), chloramphenicol (30 microg/ml), or kanamycin (50 microg/ml) where appropriate. For induction of sigma54 under the control of the anhydrotetracycline (aTc)-regulated promoter, aTc was added at a concentration of 100 ng/ml as described previously (22,23).
###end p 12
###begin p 13
###xml 0 16 0 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 323 326 317 320 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 495 496 485 486 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 533 534 523 524 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</sup>
###xml 847 849 817 819 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 857 861 827 831 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 939 941 909 911 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 0 16 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
Escherichia coli MG1655 WT strain as well as derived deletion mutant strains were grown overnight in MOPS minimal media at 37degreesC in an air shaker with vigorous aeration (225 r.p.m.). Two microliters of the overnight culture was used to inoculate 100 ml of fresh MOPS minimal medium. When the culture density reached OD600 0.2, a 1000 microl portion of culture was harvested into a prechilled 1.5 ml Eppendoff tube and then immediately put on ice for 1 min before being centrifuged at 10 000g (12 000 r.p.m. for BECKMAN MicrofugeR) for 10 min at 4degreesC. The supernatant was removed and the cell pellet resuspended immediately in 40 microl lysis buffer (1x SDS) and heated at 75degreesC for 5 min to quickly lyse the cells and prevent changes in the intracellular levels of the sigma factors being measured. We confirmed the absence of sigma54 in the rpoN deletion strain by Western blot analysis using a monoclonal antibody (6RN3) (24).
###end p 13
###begin p 14
###xml 24 26 20 22 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 32 33 24 25 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</sup>
###xml 77 79 65 67 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 85 86 69 70 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</sup>
###xml 104 106 88 90 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 107 109 91 93 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 174 176 154 156 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 344 346 320 322 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 352 353 324 325 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</sup>
###xml 370 372 342 344 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 373 375 345 347 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
Instead of using a sigma32/sigmaF-inducible strain as shown in previous sigma32/sigmaF regulon studies (22,23), we used strains carrying a plasmid with an aTc-inducible sigma54 gene in this work. The same experimental procedures for induction, collection and treatment of sample were performed as described below and in more detail in our sigma32/sigmaF regulon papers (22,23).
###end p 14
###begin title 15
RNA isolation, cDNA synthesis, labeling and hybridization for microarray experiments
###end title 15
###begin p 16
###xml 56 63 56 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 345 346 339 340 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">9</sup>
###xml 425 428 419 422 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 529 531 519 521 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 735 736 725 726 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 56 63 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
For preparing the total RNA for microarray experiments, E. coli strains were grown overnight in MOPS minimal media at 37degreesC in an air shaker with vigorous aeration (225 r.p.m.). Two microliters of the overnight culture was used to inoculate 100 ml of fresh MOPS minimal medium. A total of 15 ml samples of culture (corresponding to 7.5 x 109 cells) were taken for wild-type and mutant strains when the culture density OD600 value reached 0.2 and the same amount of culture was taken before and 5 min after induction in sigma54-overexpression strains. RNA was stabilized immediately by mixing with a double volume of RNAprotect Bacterial Reagent (Qiagen) and incubated at room temperature for 10 min. Cells were centrifuged at 5800g for 20 min and cell pellets were stored at -80degreesC prior to RNA extraction.
###end p 16
###begin p 17
###xml 986 987 982 983 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</sup>
###xml 987 994 983 990 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
Total nucleic acid was isolated using MasterPure kits (Epicentre) as described by the manufacturer. DNase I (Epicentre) was used to remove genomic DNA contamination. Total RNA was purified, precipitated and resuspended in diethylpyrocarbonate (DEPC)-treated water. The quality and integrity of the isolated RNA was checked by visualizing the 23S and 16S rRNA bands on a 2% agarose gel. A 10 microg of total RNA was mixed with 500 ng random hexamers and then was reverse transcribed for first strand cDNA by using the Superscript II system (Invitrogen). RNA was removed by using RNase H (Life Technologies) and RNase A (Epicentre). cDNA was purified by using Qiaquick PCR purification kit (Qiagen) and followed by partial DNase I digestion to fragment cDNA to an average length of 50-100 bp. The fragmented cDNA was 3'-end-labeled by using terminal transferase (New England Biolabs) and biotin-N6-ddATP (PerkinElmer) and was added to hybridization solution to load on Affymetrix GeneChipRE. coli Antisense Genome Arrays. Hybridization was carried out at 45degreesC for 16 h. The arrays were then washed and subsequently stained with streptavidin, biotin-bound anti-streptavidin antibody and streptavidin-phycoerythrin (Molecular Probes) to enhance the signal. Arrays were scanned at 570 nm with 3 microm resolution using a confocal laser scanner.
###end p 17
###begin title 18
Data analysis
###end title 18
###begin p 19
###xml 223 224 221 222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 524 525 522 523 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 592 593 590 591 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
Image analysis was carried out by Affymetrix(R) Microarry Suite 5.0 software. Cell intensity files were first generated from the image data files. An absolute expression analysis then computes the detection call, detection P-value and signal (background-subtracted and adjusted for noise) for each gene. Genes were considered up-regulated relative to the 0 time point (before induction)/wild-type strain sample if they had a 2-fold or greater increase in signal intensity and the signal intensity in the experiment had a log2 value of at least 8.0 and a detect level equal one; the higher log2 intensity values were used to limit the analysis to those genes for which we have a high degree of confidence in their level of expression.
###end p 19
###begin title 20
Array design
###end title 20
###begin p 21
###xml 16 23 14 21 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 115 122 113 120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
###xml 385 390 383 388 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B25 B26 B27">25&#8211;27</xref>
###xml 476 483 474 481 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 16 23 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 476 483 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The GeneChip(R) E. coli Antisense Genome Array was purchased from Affymetrix (catalog number: 900381). It contains in situ synthesized probe sets to detect the antisense strand of more than 4200 known open reading frames and over 1350 intergenic regions. A given gene is represented by 15 different 25-mer oligonucleotides that are designed to be complementary to the target sequence (25-27). Sequence information for probes on the array corresponds to the M54 version of the E. coli Genome Project database at the University of Wisconsin. Complete array information, including the location for each feature on the array, can be found at .
###end p 21
###begin title 22
Purification and fluorescence labeling of proteins and MAbs for immunoblot assay
###end title 22
###begin p 23
###xml 43 50 43 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 94 100 94 100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 102 104 102 104 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B28">28</xref>
###xml 197 203 197 203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 205 207 205 207 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 270 278 270 278 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 373 375 366 368 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 437 439 426 428 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 619 621 608 610 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B29">29</xref>
###xml 825 827 814 816 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 828 830 817 819 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 43 50 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 301 306 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
Purified core RNA polymerase was made from E. coli MG1655 according to the method of Thompson et al. (28). Purified sigma factors and monoclonal antibodies (MAbs) were made as described in Anthony et al. (24). Purified core RNA polymerase and sigma factors were used in in vitro transcription assays. Mouse MAbs used in this experiment were anti-beta' (NT73) and anti-sigma54 (6RN3) for measuring the intracellular level changes of sigma54. Both MAbs are available from Neoclone (Madison, WI, USA). Fluorescent dye, IC5-OSu (Dojindo), was used to label the primary antibodies according to previously described methods (29). The IC5-labeled MAbs, at final stored concentrations of 1 mg/ml, were diluted 1: 2000 for use in this experiment. Electrophoresis and immunoblot assays were performed as described in a previous paper (22,23). Signal intensities of the bands obtained with the Molecular Dynamics Typhoon system were quantified using the ImageQuant program.
###end p 23
###begin title 24
Chromatin immunoprecipitation assays
###end title 24
###begin p 25
###xml 126 133 126 133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 231 233 231 233 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B30">30</xref>
###xml 234 236 234 236 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31">31</xref>
###xml 242 249 242 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 429 436 429 436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 611 613 611 613 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31">31</xref>
###xml 773 775 772 774 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 827 829 826 828 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B33">33</xref>
###xml 857 865 856 864 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 925 927 924 926 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B34">34</xref>
###xml 928 930 927 929 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B35">35</xref>
###xml 242 249 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Chromatin immunoprecipitation (ChIP) assay is usually used to crosslink proteins to adjacent DNA by adding formaldehyde to an in vivo culture. Recently, the Aseem Ansari group at UW-Madison has developed the current ChIP protocol (30,31) for E. coli studies. To map promoters in bacteria, they sought a way to force RNAP to reside only at promoters so that identifying DNA fragments bound to a given sigma factor associated RNAP in vivo would report promoter locations. A variety of small-molecule inhibitors of RNA polymerase were evaluated for the immobilization of RNAP, and rifampin was found to work best (31). The antibiotic rifampin inhibits bacterial growth by binding the ss-subunit of RNAP near the active site, blocking the synthesis of RNAs longer than 2-3 nt (32). Rifampin has no effect on RNAP promoter binding (33) and has no effect on RNAP in vitro when added after elongating RNAP has cleared the promoter (34,35).
###end p 25
###begin p 26
###xml 52 54 48 50 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 138 140 130 132 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 628 630 610 612 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 809 811 781 783 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
The general procedures for the confirmation of sigma54-dependent genes are: cross-linked chromatin is isolated from rifampin-treated sigma54 overexpression and deletion cells, cells were then resuspended in 500 ml lysis buffer [10 mM Tris-HCl (pH 8.0), 50 mM NaCl] with 3 mg/ml lysozyme and incubated for 30 min at 37degreesC. A 500 ml of 2 x IP buffer [200 mM Tris-HCl (pH 8.0), 600 mM NaCl, 4% Triton X-100] was added and the DNA was sheared by sonication. Cell debris was removed by centrifugation, and the supernatant was transferred to new tubes. The samples were immunoprecipitated with monoclonal antibodies against sigma54 (6RN3) (NeoClone, Madison, WI, USA). The immunoprecipitated protein-DNA crosslinks are then reversed at 65degreesC overnight. The ChIP DNA served as template for amplifying sigma54-dependent promoters by PCR.
###end p 26
###begin title 27
Primer extension assays
###end title 27
###begin p 28
###xml 201 203 196 198 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 251 253 246 248 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 691 692 674 675 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 543 546 <span type="species:ncbi:11866?0.5863095238095238|species:ncbi:12321?0.21726190476190477">AMV</span>
###xml 611 614 <span type="species:ncbi:11866?0.5863095238095238|species:ncbi:12321?0.21726190476190477">AMV</span>
The total RNA was prepared as described in microarray experiments above. The primer (5'-GTTGCGATAAGCTGCAA) was 5'-end-labeled using T4 polynucleotide kinase (New England Biolabs) and 50 muCi of [gamma-32P]-ATP (PerkinElmer). Approximately 1.5 pmol of 32P-end-labeled oligonucleotide was added to the reaction. To denature nucleic acids, the reactions were heated at 95degreesC for 3 min and quenched on wet ice. An incubation step at 50degreesC for 15 min was done to promote annealing of the oligonucleotide to the RNA template. Two units of AMV Reverse Transcriptase (Promega) and final concentrations of 1 x AMV Reverse Transcriptase buffer [50 mM Tris-HCl (pH 8.3), 50 mM KCl, 10 mM MgCl2, 0.5 mM spermidine, 10 mM dithiothreitol (Promega)], and 0.2 mM each of the four deoxynucleoside triphosphates were added to each reaction tube. Reaction mixtures were incubated at 42degreesC for 90 min. Primer extension products were electrophoresed on a 5% denaturing polyacrylamide gel. The gel was dried, exposed in a phosphorimaging cassette, and scanned by using a Molecular Dynamics Typhoon (Model 8600).
###end p 28
###begin title 29
RESULTS
###end title 29
###begin title 30
###xml 18 20 14 16 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 24 31 20 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 24 31 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The level of sigma54 in E. coli MG1655 derivative deletion and overexpression strains
###end title 30
###begin p 31
###xml 0 16 0 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 22 24 18 20 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 67 69 59 61 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 131 137 123 129 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 139 141 131 133 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 142 144 134 136 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 304 306 292 294 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 526 527 511 512 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 528 530 513 515 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B36">36</xref>
###xml 657 665 642 650 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 687 689 668 670 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 717 725 698 706 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 735 739 716 720 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 804 806 781 783 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1013 1015 975 977 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 1016 1018 978 980 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 1032 1034 990 992 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 1044 1045 998 999 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</sup>
###xml 1218 1222 1168 1172 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ltet</sub>
###xml 1319 1322 1269 1272 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 1421 1430 1367 1376 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 1.</label>
###xml 1453 1455 1395 1397 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1477 1481 1419 1423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 1507 1509 1445 1447 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1555 1556 1493 1494 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</bold>
###xml 1598 1600 1529 1531 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1662 1666 1593 1597 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 1824 1826 1748 1750 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1891 1895 1815 1819 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 1945 1946 1869 1870 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>
###xml 1985 1987 1902 1904 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 2081 2083 1994 1996 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1430 2228 1376 2129 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="32">Determination the &#963;<sup>54</sup> protein level in the <italic>rpoN</italic> deletion (KZ30) and &#963;<sup>54</sup> overexpression (KZ7) strains, respectively. (<bold>A</bold>) Western blot analysis of &#946;&#8242; and &#963;<sup>54</sup> protein expression in the wild-type MG1655 as well as in the <italic>rpoN</italic> deletion strains. Expression of &#946;&#8242; subunit of core RNA polymerase, which served as internal controls, can be detected in both strains. Expression of &#963;<sup>54</sup> can only be detected in wild-type strain, but the expression of <italic>rpoN</italic> gene is absent in the respective mutant strain. (<bold>B</bold>) Left: western blot of &#946;&#8242; and &#963;<sup>54</sup> expression before and 5 min after induction. Right: quantification of western blot. The &#963;<sup>54</sup> protein level increases &#8764;2.9-fold after 5 min of induction. Signal intensities are determined using ImageQuant version 5.2 software.</p>

###xml 0 16 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
Escherichia coli sigma54 in-frame deletion strains as well as sigma54-overexpression strains were constructed as described in Zhao et al. (22,23) and in Experimental procedures section. A fast and reliable improved western blot assay was used for quantitative analysis of the intracellular level of sigma54 in the in-frame deletion and overexpression strains. The beta'-subunit of core RNA polymerase was also examined to serve as an internal control because its intracellular levels remain constant under various conditions (9,36). The signal intensities of the proteins were immunodetected by corresponding IC5-labeled monoclonal antibodies. Our results (Figure 1A) show that the sigma54 protein was not expressed (Figure 1A) in the rpoN deletion strain, confirming inactivation of this gene. The sigma54 protein level, which is normalized to the beta' subunit of RNA polymerase, rapidly increased 5 min after induction with an approximately2.9-fold change. Using the same overexpression system, previous data (22,23) showed sigma32 and sigmaF protein levels after 5 minutes induction increased almost 7.4- and 2.3-fold, respectively. The discrepancy of the fold changes, for different sigma factors under the same PLtet promoter control, is mainly due to the fact that the experiments were performed at log-phase (OD600 = 0.2) in minimum medium, in which different sigma factors have different initial protein levels. Figure 1.Determination the sigma54 protein level in the rpoN deletion (KZ30) and sigma54 overexpression (KZ7) strains, respectively. (A) Western blot analysis of beta' and sigma54 protein expression in the wild-type MG1655 as well as in the rpoN deletion strains. Expression of beta' subunit of core RNA polymerase, which served as internal controls, can be detected in both strains. Expression of sigma54 can only be detected in wild-type strain, but the expression of rpoN gene is absent in the respective mutant strain. (B) Left: western blot of beta' and sigma54 expression before and 5 min after induction. Right: quantification of western blot. The sigma54 protein level increases approximately2.9-fold after 5 min of induction. Signal intensities are determined using ImageQuant version 5.2 software.
###end p 31

###begin title 33
###xml 11 13 7 9 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
Known sigma54-dependent promoters
###end title 33
###begin p 34
###xml 65 67 61 63 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 82 89 78 85 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 233 235 225 227 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 279 282 271 274 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 620 624 606 610 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 668 670 650 652 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
To characterize the effect of the decreasing and increasing sigma54 protein level in vivo on gene expression, global RNA transcript abundance was monitored in the deletion mutant strain and the overexpression strain 5 min after sigma54 induction with cells grown in log-phase (OD600 = 0.2) in MOPS minimal medium at 37degreesC. Transcription profiles were obtained as described in 'Experimental procedures' section. The sample for the wild-type strain and for the overexpression strain at time zero before induction was used as the reference to identify genes whose transcript abundance had significantly changed in the rpoN deletion mutant strain or the induced sigma54-overexpression strain, respectively.
###end p 34

textid="43"><sup>g</sup>The first gene in a known or predicted multicistronic operon.</p></fn></table-wrap-foot></table-wrap>
DNA microarray results showed the transcriptional level of all well-characterized genes belonging to the sigma54 regulon are downregulated/upregulated in the rpoN deletion strain/sigma54 overexpression strain (Table 1). These results are consistent with our previous hypothesis that a change of the intracellular level of a given sigma factor will cause a change of the transcriptional level of genes dependent on this sigma factor. Jishage (9) reported that the intracellular level of sigma54 is maintained at 16% or 6% the level of sigma70 during log and stationary phase growth, respectively, in two different strains. Loss of sigma54 in cells will decrease the transcription of sigma54-dependent genes. Induction of sigma54 will show an increase in the transcriptional level of sigma54-dependent genes. ###begin p 44
###xml 78 80 74 76 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 84 91 80 87 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 291 295 287 291 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 396 398 388 390 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 491 493 479 481 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 84 91 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
There are 18 known promoters (controlling 52 genes) under the control of sigma54 in E. coli. Using a stringent cut off (2-fold decrease/increase to reduce the potential noise caused by array signal variation), 15 out of these 18 promoters significantly downregulated its operon genes in the rpoN deletion strain and 13 out of these 18 significantly upregulated their controlled genes in the sigma54 overexpression strain. This indicates our microarray experiments can detect most known sigma54-dependent promoters in our assays.
###end p 44

###xml 85 92 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Expression profiling of transcripts corresponding to the complete set of ORFs in the E. coli genome revealed that the response to the changes of sigma54in vivo was quite broad. In addition to identifying the known sigma54-dependent genes, our microarray data allowed us to assign many additional new candidate genes to the sigma54 regulon. Comparative analysis of the microarray data from the set of genes whose transcription is downregulated in the rpoN deletion strain (decrease of sigma54) and the set of genes with increased transcription at 5 minutes after sigma54 induction (increase of sigma54) allows us to narrow down to 22 new candidate genes with high confidence in the sigma54 regulon (Table 2). Results from promoter region consensus analysis using the algorithms MEME (37) and BioProspector (38) revealed the upstream regulatory sequences of most newly identified genes have a good match with the previously known sigma54 consensus binding site (Table 2). ###begin p 55
###xml 41 43 37 39 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 106 108 98 100 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 166 173 158 165 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 187 191 179 183 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ibpB</italic>
###xml 295 297 283 285 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 299 301 287 289 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B39">39</xref>
###xml 333 337 321 325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dnaK</italic>
###xml 432 434 416 418 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 444 446 424 426 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 463 465 439 441 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 477 479 453 455 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
To further confirm new genes in the sigma54 regulon, we performed ChIP assays to test the binding of sigma54-associated holoenzyme to promoter regions of these genes in vivo. We used the ibpB gene as positive control for the ChIP assay because this gene is known to be under the control of sigma54 (39). The upstream sequence of the dnaK gene was chosen as a negative control because transcription of this gene is regulated by sigma70 and sigma32 but is not sigma54-dependent (40).
###end p 55

###xml 335 339 315 319 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dnaK</italic>
###xml 381 383 357 359 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 411 413 383 385 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 443 445 411 413 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>

###xml 488 490 452 454 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 644 652 608 616 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>

###xml 853 1570 809 1494 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="57">Chromatin immunoprecipitation assays to test the DNA fragments carrying putative &#963;<sup>54</sup> promoter element(s). ###xml 844 1570 800 1494 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F2" position="float"><label>Figure 2.</label><caption><p textid="57">Chromatin immunoprecipitation assays to test the DNA fragments carrying putative &#963;<sup>54</sup> promoter element(s). Using specific monoclonal antibodies (mAb) against sigma54, immunoprecipitation (ChIP) assays show the ibpB gene's promoter DNA sequence can be pulled down by anti-sigma54 mAb in sigma54 overexpression strain, but not in sigma54 deletion strain due to lack of functional sigma54. For the negative control, the promoter DNA sequence of dnaK cannot be pulled down in either the sigma54 overexpression or the sigma54 deletion strain by anti-sigma54 mAb in vivo because the gene lacks a sigma54 promoter in its regulatory region. In addition, our ChIP assays show that 8 out of 10 of the newly identified genes' promoter DNA fragments (as shown in Figure 2) can be directly pulled-down in the sigma54-overexpression strain and not in the sigma54-deletion strain. This indicates that most genes identified by our microarray experiments are genuine. Figure 2.Chromatin immunoprecipitation assays to test the DNA fragments carrying putative sigma54 promoter element(s). (A) ibpB served as a positive control and dnaK is serve as negative control. ChIPs assays are performed by using specific monoclonal antibody against sigma54 (6RN3). The experiments are performed in both sigma54 overexpression (left) and sigma54 deletion (right) strains, respectively. The samples of DNA fragments containing sigma54-dependent promoters were immunoprecipitated by monoclonal antibodies against sigma54. (B) Potential sigma54 consensus binding sites of each gene are predicted and aligned by computer program. The previously known sigma54 two-block promoter element consensus is shown below.
###end p 56

###begin p 58
###xml 40 42 36 38 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 78 85 74 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 116 118 108 110 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 146 148 134 136 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 216 218 200 202 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 262 264 242 244 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">70</sup>
###xml 445 447 425 427 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 78 85 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
In a separate study, we identified sigma70 targets comprehensively across the E. coli genome. We compare those sigma70 target genes with the sigma54-dependent genes identified in this study. We found 14% of the sigma54-dependent genes can be transcribed by sigma70-associated RNAP (unpublished data), indicating bacteria use different promoter organizations to produce different regulatory outcomes under the appropriate environment conditions (41).
###end p 58

###xml 946 947 942 943 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">(</sub>
###xml 947 948 943 944 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>

###xml 1142 1143 1134 1135 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</sub>
###xml 1206 1208 1194 1196 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1220 1221 1208 1209 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>

###xml 1333 1335 1313 1315 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>

###xml 1435 1437 1411 1413 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>
###xml 1483 1485 1455 1457 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1554 1556 1526 1528 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B42">42</xref>
###xml 1307 1729 1291 1701 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="61">Determination of the &#963;<sup>54</sup> consensus binding site. &#963;<sup>54</sup>-related two-block promoter element is aligned using Bioprospector (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>) from the upstream sequence of genes in &#963;<sup>54</sup> regulon identified in our assays and displayed using SEQUENCE LOGO (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B42">42</xref>). ###xml 1307 1729 1291 1701 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><p textid="61">Determination of the &#963;<sup>54</sup> consensus binding site. &#963;<sup>54</sup>-related two-block promoter element is aligned using Bioprospector (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>) from the upstream sequence of genes in &#963;<sup>54</sup> regulon identified in our assays and displayed using SEQUENCE LOGO (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B42">42</xref>). The height of each column reflects the non-random bias of particular residues at that position, the size of each residue letter reflecting its frequency at that position.</p></caption>
###xml 1729 1729 1701 1701 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkp1123f3"/>
###xml 1298 1729 1282 1701 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F3" position="float"><label>Figure 3.</label><caption><p textid="61">Determination of the &#963;<sup>54</sup> consensus binding site. &#963;<sup>54</sup>-related two-block promoter element is aligned using Bioprospector (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>) from the upstream sequence of genes in &#963;<sup>54</sup> regulon identified in our assays and displayed using SEQUENCE LOGO (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B42">42</xref>). The height of each column reflects the non-random bias of particular residues at that position, the size of each residue letter reflecting its frequency at that position.</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="gkp1123f3"/></fig>
A computer program was used to examine upstream DNA sequence of upregulated genes in our microarray data to look for regulatory sequence motifs. As prokaryotic promoter motifs often occur in two blocks with a gap of variable length, BioProspector (38), a C program which is capable of modeling motifs with two blocks and uses a Gibbs sampling strategy, was used to find the -12 and -24 consensus regions for sigma54 binding. Upstream sequences (400 bases from the first genes in transcription units that contain 2-fold up-regulated/down-regulated genes in our microarray data) were extracted as input sequences. A number of overall highest scoring motifs as position- specific probability matrices were reported. According to the reported highest scoring motif and its site locations on the input sequence, a graphical display of the results was generated using SEQUENCE LOGO (42) (Figure 3). The resulting consensus is represented as a TGGca-(N)(4-5)-ttGCaa, where lower case indicates a less highly conserved site. This consensus agrees well with previously reported Esigma54 consensus which was aligned to maximize alignment (TGGcacg-(N)4-5-tGCtat) in the -24 and -12 regions of several published Esigma54 promoters (3,43-45), indicating the conservation of sigma54 promoter across these genes. Figure 3.Determination of the sigma54 consensus binding site. sigma54-related two-block promoter element is aligned using Bioprospector (38) from the upstream sequence of genes in sigma54 regulon identified in our assays and displayed using SEQUENCE LOGO (42). The height of each column reflects the non-random bias of particular residues at that position, the size of each residue letter reflecting its frequency at that position.
###end p 60

###xml 453 458 453 458 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B49 B50 B51">49&#8211;51</xref>
###xml 554 556 550 552 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>

###xml 905 907 897 899 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B52">52</xref>
###xml 935 948 927 940 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 953 974 945 966 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Neisseria gonorrhoeae</italic>
###xml 976 978 968 970 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B53">53</xref>
###xml 1057 1059 1045 1047 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1075 1082 1063 1070 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 159 166 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 171 193 <span type="species:ncbi:90371">Salmonella typhimurium</span>
###xml 249 271 <span type="species:ncbi:155892">Caulobacter crescentus</span>
###xml 368 383 <span type="species:ncbi:666">Vibrio cholerae</span>
###xml 385 407 <span type="species:ncbi:287">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</span>
###xml 412 426 <span type="species:ncbi:294">P. fluorescens</span>
###xml 874 881 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 886 900 <span type="species:ncbi:90371">S. typhimurium</span>
###xml 935 948 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 953 974 <span type="species:ncbi:485">Neisseria gonorrhoeae</span>
###xml 1075 1082 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
In Gram-negative bacteria, the hierarchy of the flagellar regulatory system has been well characterized in micro-organisms with peritrichous flagella, such as E. coli and Salmonella typhimurium (46,47) and polar flagellated micro-organisms, such as Caulobacter crescentus (48). Recently, the regulatory cascade components of bacteria with one polar flagellum, such as Vibrio cholerae, Pseudomonas aeruginosa and P. fluorescens, have been characterized (49-51). The regulators at the top of the polar flagellar hierarchy belong to the NtrC family of sigma54-associated transcription activators. This regulator, together with sigma54, activates the expression of genes in polar flagellar system. In addition to its role in flagellar gene expression in these bacteria, this alternative sigma factor is known to participate in transcription of genes in nitrogen assimilation in E. coli and S. typhimurium (11,52) and in pilin synthesis in P. aeruginosa and Neisseria gonorrhoeae (53). No experiments have been performed and reported to test whether or not sigma54 is involved in E. coli flagellar biosynthesis.
###end p 63
###begin p 64
###xml 87 91 87 91 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 166 170 166 170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 265 273 265 273 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 383 387 383 387 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 526 531 526 531 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B54 B55 B56 B57">54&#8211;57</xref>
###xml 558 560 554 556 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 815 817 807 809 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 907 909 895 897 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1008 1017 996 1005 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4.</label>
###xml 1029 1036 1017 1024 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1055 1059 1043 1047 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 1124 1128 1112 1116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 1232 1239 1220 1227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1259 1261 1243 1245 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1283 1287 1267 1271 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 1017 1293 1005 1277 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="65">Motility in <italic>E. coli</italic> wild-type and the <italic>rpoN</italic> deletion strains. Compared with wild-type strain, disruption of <italic>rpoN</italic> causes impaired movement on a swarm plate. The motility can be complemented from this mutant strain by <italic>in vivo</italic> expression of &#963;<sup>54</sup> from a plasmid-borne <italic>rpoN</italic> gene.</p>
###xml 1017 1293 1005 1277 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><p textid="65">Motility in <italic>E. coli</italic> wild-type and the <italic>rpoN</italic> deletion strains. ###xml 1293 1293 1277 1277 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkp1123f4"/>
###xml 1008 1293 996 1277 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F4" position="float"><label>Figure 4.</label><caption><p textid="65">Motility in <italic>E. coli</italic> wild-type and the <italic>rpoN</italic> deletion strains. Compared with wild-type strain, disruption of <italic>rpoN</italic> causes impaired movement on a swarm plate. The motility can be complemented from this mutant strain by <italic>in vivo</italic> expression of &#963;<sup>54</sup> from a plasmid-borne <italic>rpoN</italic> gene.</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="gkp1123f4"/></fig>
###xml 1029 1036 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
To investigate this hypothesis, we first compared the motility of wild-type strain and rpoN in-frame deletion strain by growing them on the swarm plate. We found the rpoN null mutant significantly reduces its motility compared with its derivative wild-type strain (Figure 4). Our microarray data also showed a significantly down-regulation of the transcription of flagellar genes in rpoN in-frame deletion strain (). Because the expression of the FlhDC operon can be regulated by multiple positive and negative regulators () (54-57), we checked whether sigma54 affects the expression of these regulators and thus indirectly affects flhDC operon expression. Our microarray data show the expression of most negative regulators is downregulated and the expression of most positive regulators is upregulated () in sigma54 deletion strain. Therefore, the downshifting of expression of the flhDC gene in the sigma54 deletion strain is not primarily due to the level changes of those regulators in the same strain. Figure 4.Motility in E. coli wild-type and the rpoN deletion strains. Compared with wild-type strain, disruption of rpoN causes impaired movement on a swarm plate. The motility can be complemented from this mutant strain by in vivo expression of sigma54 from a plasmid-borne rpoN gene.
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 12 19 12 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 38 42 38 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 107 111 107 111 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 215 222 215 222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 242 244 238 240 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 266 270 262 266 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 12 19 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Motility in E. coli wild-type and the rpoN deletion strains. Compared with wild-type strain, disruption of rpoN causes impaired movement on a swarm plate. The motility can be complemented from this mutant strain by in vivo expression of sigma54 from a plasmid-borne rpoN gene.
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 40 47 40 47 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 102 109 102 109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 119 121 119 121 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B58">58</xref>
###xml 586 588 582 584 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 40 47 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 102 109 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The Matsumura group found the sequenced E. coli strain MG1655 is extremely motile compared with other E. coli strains (58). Sequence analysis shows that there are mobile elements, insA-5 and insB-5, inserted into the upstream regulatory region of flhDC operon. They proposed that the high motility of MG1655 is due to insertion element insB-5, which prevents binding of the negative regulator OmpR, and thus increase the expression of flhDC operon for flagellar synthesis (). We think we can provide an alternative explanation for at least some of this high motility phenomenon; a sigma54-dependent promoter has been brought in by this insertion element.
###end p 66

A bioinformatics approach (38) has been used to search the sigma54 consensus binding site in the upstream regulatory region of flhDC operon. A good match of a sigma54-dependent promoter has been found in this insB-5 insertion element (Figure 5A). RT-PCR as described in previous paper (22,23) (PrimerUp: 5'-GCATGACAAAGTCATCGG, PrimerDown: 5'-GTTGCGATAAGCTGCAA) has been performed and showed that there is an additional transcript from the upstream region of the known sigma70-dependent promoter on this operon (Figure 5B). Primer extension assays showed this transcript present in the sigma54-overexpression strain but not in the sigma54-deletion strain (as shown in Figure 5C), indicating it was transcribed from a sigma54-dependent promoter that was brought in by the insB-5 insertion element. The biological significance of this is discussed below. Figure 5.Evidence indicating potential new sigma54 promoter in the upstream of flhDC operon. Two-block binding site for these two promoters have been selected to compare with respective known consensus promoter binding sites as shown below. (B) Total RNA was prepared and reverse transcribed to cDNA. The primer pair as shown in (A) was used to amplify the transcripts starting from upstream of the sigma70-dependent promoter in the regulative region of the flhDC operon. (C) Primer extension assays have been performed in the sigma54-overxpression strain and deletion strain. A sigma54-dependent transcript is present in the sigma54 overexpression strain and is not in the sigma54 deletion strain. The sigma70-dependent transcript can be detected in both lanes.
