###begin title 69
DISCUSSION
###end title 69
###begin p 70
###xml 300 307 296 303 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 300 307 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Transcription is a key control point for regulation of numerous cellular activities. Bacteria regulate levels of gene expression by using transcription factors that modulate the recruitment of RNAP to promoter elements in the DNA. Because sigma factors are required to initiate gene transcription in E. coli, and there are different sigma factors required to regulate different sets of genes or regulons to adapt to changes in external environment, determination of sigma regulons will provide valuable information for classifying genes into different functional groups and will be the first essential step to understanding global gene regulation under different growth conditions.
###end p 70
###begin p 71
###xml 76 78 72 74 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 78 85 74 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 189 191 181 183 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 247 249 235 237 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 271 275 259 263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 361 365 349 353 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ltet</sub>
###xml 415 417 399 401 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 421 425 405 409 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpoN</italic>
###xml 504 506 484 486 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 566 568 542 544 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 654 656 626 628 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 726 728 694 696 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 913 915 877 879 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1148 1150 1106 1108 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1266 1268 1220 1222 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1282 1289 1236 1243 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1547 1549 1497 1499 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1569 1578 1519 1528 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in silico</italic>
###xml 1763 1765 1709 1711 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1882 1887 1828 1833 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B59 B60 B61 B62">59&#8211;62</xref>
###xml 1993 1995 1935 1937 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1282 1289 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The aim of the present work is to identify promoters under control of Esigma54in vivo. Under defined, steady-state growth conditions, we used two different genetic approaches to alter sigma54 concentration in cells: (i) moderately expressing sigma54 from a plasmid-borne rpoN gene controlled by anhydrotetracycline (aTc)-inducible and Tet repressor-controlled PLtet promoter; (ii) disrupting the expression of sigma54 in rpoN deletion mutant strains. These combined methodologies used to determine Esigma54 promoters proved highly effective as nearly all known sigma54-dependent promoters were identified. Our analysis has identified 40 targets of Esigma54, including 22 previously undescribed targets. This is far more Esigma54 promoters than expected. We chose a stringent cutoff (less than 2-fold change) when analyzing the microarray data to ensure that almost all called targets are genuine targets of Esigma54. Our site validation and ChIP assays confirms that most, if not all, are genuine. We repeated our analysis using a less stringent cutoff (>/=1.5-fold). In this case, we identified an additional 30 target regions () with strong sigma54-like promoter in its upstream regulation region. On the basis of this analysis, we estimate that there are 70 sigma54 promoters in E. coli, almost four times the number of previously identified promoters. Around 20% of the newly identified genes are hypothetical and the role of these genes remains to be elucidated. To obtain a better understanding of consensus binding sites controlled by sigma54, we carried out an in silico analysis on the presence of -24/-12 type promoters in the upstream region of these genes. Under the condition of our experiment, we think the expression of some of the identified sigma54-depenedent targets might be just a small fraction of the maximum due to strict dependence on AAA-family activators (59-62) some of whose activities might be limiting in our experiments. Likewise, it is possible that a few sigma54-dependent targets will be missed in our experiments due to very low or no activities of certain AAA-family activators.
###end p 71
###begin p 72
###xml 55 62 55 62 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 120 122 116 118 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 216 221 212 217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flhDC</italic>
###xml 381 383 373 375 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 403 410 395 402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 860 862 852 854 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B63">63</xref>
###xml 889 891 877 879 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1210 1212 1194 1196 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1368 1370 1348 1350 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1446 1459 1426 1439 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. crescentus</italic>
###xml 1461 1463 1441 1443 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B48">48</xref>
###xml 1466 1489 1446 1469 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rhodobacter sphaeroides</italic>
###xml 1491 1496 1471 1476 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B64 B65 B66">64&#8211;66</xref>
###xml 1499 1518 1479 1498 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter pylori</italic>
###xml 1520 1522 1500 1502 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B67">67</xref>
###xml 1528 1548 1508 1528 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Campylobacter jejuni</italic>
###xml 1550 1552 1530 1532 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B68">68</xref>
###xml 1684 1686 1660 1662 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">54</sup>
###xml 1702 1709 1678 1685 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 55 62 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1446 1459 <span type="species:ncbi:155892">C. crescentus</span>
###xml 1466 1489 <span type="species:ncbi:1063">Rhodobacter sphaeroides</span>
###xml 1499 1518 <span type="species:ncbi:210">Helicobacter pylori</span>
###xml 1528 1548 <span type="species:ncbi:197">Campylobacter jejuni</span>
###xml 1702 1709 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
We characterized an alternative strategy for sequenced E. coli strain MG1655 flagellar biosynthesis. In this case, sigma54-dependent promoter is brought by an insertion element into the upstream regulatory region of flhDC operon which encodes FlhDC, the master regulator for flagellar biosynthesis. Primer extension assays show there is a transcript transcribed from this new sigma54-dependent promoter in vivo. This also provides additional explanation for the high motility of this strain compared with other related bacteria. Lateral gene transfer is a major factor in the evolution of bacteria. Bacteria genomes contain a significant number of mobile elements-DNA that can move around on chromosomes, among organisms and even between species. It has been reported that mobile DNA can carry genes for virulence and drug resistance, as well as benign genes (63). The discovery of a sigma54-dependent promoter in a motile element in our work might provide another paradigm for the horizontal exchange of genetic information in prokaryotes. This additional fluidity allows bacteria to turn on different genes in various conditions to enhance their ability to survival or cause disease. The implication of sigma54 involvement in bacterial motility regulation is widespread in Gram-negative bacteria. Indeed, the elements of flagellar regulatory cascades including sigma54-associated regulators have also been identified in micro-organisms such as C. crescentus (48), Rhodobacter sphaeroides (64-66), Helicobacter pylori (67) and Campylobacter jejuni (68). Although environmental and genetic factors that control dissemination of these mobile elements remain to be determined, the sigma54 involvement in E. coli MG1655 flagellar biosynthesis might indicate a remarkable rearrangement/improvement in the functional organization of regulatory mechanisms that has existed in its other close-related bacteria. This might also indicate an evolutionary conservation among Gram-negative bacteria.
###end p 72
